        <h3>
         Top 13 Sites For Independent Filmmakers
        </h3>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
    </div>

		&lt;p&gt;In recent years, the content of the internet has transformed itself from a controlled and manufactured environment to a vast expanse of user generated content. Internet users can log on and create their own subjects, themes, and arguments to the sites they frequent. This idea gave birth to sites like Facebook, and Twitter; as well as creating tools like wikis, forums, and blogs. This new type of social media forged specific online communities where people with similar interests could share and collaborate freely on ideas.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Independent filmmakers have an ever-growing presence on social media sites such as twitter, facebook, youtube, and various blogs. This presence has resulted in a wealth of shared knowledge for filmmakers worldwide. These sites have become a hub for the independent filmmaking community, and are a vital resource many young writers, directors, and producers alike.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Heres a list of thirteen sites that are excellent resources for independent filmmakers in no particular order.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Filmmaker&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Filmmakers on a tight budget know perfectly well how difficult it is to stay on that budget. Filmmaker.coms blog contains helpful articles regarding a wide array of topics from industry news, to new software updates, and to helpful tips. Members of the site can post on the forums and exchange information on filmmaking as well as their own projects. The forum is an ideal place for independent filmmakers to seek knowledge from their peers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://filmmaker.com" target="_blank"&gt;Filmmaker&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Film Riot&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Film Riot is a video tutorial site with a comedic twist. Host Ryan Connolly covers every subject from how to make a music video, to using CGI, to how to cast your film. This site is a delightful departure from the typical monotonous tutorials usually found on the net as the humorous videos take a narrative structure making them actually enjoyable to watch.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://revision3.com/filmriot" target="_blank"&gt;Film Riot&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Film Riot on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/filmriot" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Check out their &lt;a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/filmriot" target="_blank"&gt;YouTube Channel&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Go Into The Story&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Good screenwriters know how important it is to know every trick of the trade there is (even if they do not use them all). Go Into The Story ditches all the fancy graphics and cluttering advertisements and opts for the bare essentials of screenwriting. Blogger Scott Myers, a screenwriting professor at the University of North Carolina, posts advice and how-to-guides daily to aid young writers in the creative process. The blog also sports an extensive list of other great websites and blogs that serve as great resource as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://www.gointothestory.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Go Into The Story&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Scott Myers on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/GoIntoTheStory" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Hope For Film&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Hope for Film is the brainchild of the American independent film producer Ted Hope. His credits include 21 Grams (2003), American Splendor (2003), and Adventureland (2009) to name a few. Everyday Hope and various guest bloggers post advice and opinions concerning independent film. Like johnaugust.com this blog is a great opportunity for beginner filmmakers to seek and discuss insight of an industry professional.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://hopeforfilm.com" target="_blank"&gt;Hope for Film&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Ted Hope on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/tedhope" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;IndieTalk&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Similar to Filmmaker.com, IndieTalk is filmmaking community in which filmmakers share and exchange ideas in a forum. The forums are broken down into categories such as Cameras &amp; Lenses, Screenwriting, Cinematography and Lighting, and Post Production. The members on the forum typically offer advice on how to get around problems in filmmaking while not doing damage to your wallet.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://www.indietalk.com" target="_blank"&gt;IndieTalk&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;IndieWire&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Similar to Twitch Film, IndieWire is convergence point filmmakers and film lovers alike. Fans of independent cinema receive information of films and festivals, as well as reviews and blogs. Filmmakers can read articles covering topics such as production, distribution, exhibition, and festival strategy.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://www.indiewire.com" target="_blank"&gt;IndieWire&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow IndieWire on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/indiewire" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;John August&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;John August is an accomplished screenwriter whose credits most notably include Tim Burtons films Big Fish (2003), Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (2005), and Corpse Bride (2005). He started his blog back in 2003 as an encyclopedia of information about screenwriting. Since then it has expanded into a wealth of information ranging from career advice to the state of the film industry itself. Many of the blog posts are responses to reader-submitted questions, making it a great way for independent writers to get feedback from a working professional.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://johnaugust.com" target="_blank"&gt;johnaugust.com&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow John August on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/johnaugust" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Raindance&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Besides being one of Britains largest independent film festivals, Raindance also offers a treasure trove of information and how-to-tips for independent filmmakers worldwide. Under the resources section of the site there are links to articles written by members of the Raindance team and industry professionals. These articles detail the tricks and traps for filmmaking on little to no budget at all. Raindance also runs a film school with am innovative &lt;a title="Postgraduate Film Degree" href="http://www.raindance.org/postgraduate-film-degree/"&gt;postgraduate film degree&lt;/a&gt; in association with Staffordshire University and the Independent Film Trust. They also have 7 regional offices in six countries which gives them an unusual and valuable perspective on new trends in independent film.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://www.raindance.co.uk/" target="_blank"&gt;Raindance&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Raindance on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/Raindance_Fest" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Shooting People&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shooting People is a network for filmmakers based out of London. It serves as a means for independent filmmakers to connect with each other by using blogs, databases, newsletters, and podcasts. Members of the site have premiered at Sundance, been nominated at BAFTA and the Oscars, and screened at Cannes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://shootingpeople.org" target="_blank"&gt;Shooting People&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Shooting People on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/shootingpeople" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Twitch Film&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The world of independent cinema is so widespread around the globe it can sometimes be difficult to absorb it all it. Twitch Film compiles everything there is to know and creates a central hub for the lovers of indie, international, and cult films. Followers of the site can read news, reviews, and interviews regarding a huge library of international and independent films; as well participate in forums and comment on articles.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a href="http://twitchfilm.com" target="_blank"&gt;Twitch Film&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Follow Twitch Film on &lt;a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/twitchfilm" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Philip Bloom&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Philip Bloom has travelled the world as a successful maker of short films, documentaries. adverts and much more. He is part of the new breed of digital cinematographers, using DLSRs to achieve that film look. On his website you can see his wide range of work, from his adverts with Kevin Spacey to his 5D Cinematography on the WWII Lucasfilm Red Tails.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View &lt;a title="Philip Bloom" href="http://www.philipbloom.net" target="_blank"&gt;philipbloom.net&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;NoFilmSchool&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;No Film School is a site for DIY filmmakers and independent creatives run by Brooklyn based filmmaker Ryan Koo. It offers solutions to how to get the most out of the things you create in order to sustain a long career as a filmmaker, writer, director, producer, editor, cinematographers and much more.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View&lt;a title="NoFIlmSchool" href="http://www.nofilmschool.com" target="_blank"&gt;nofilmschool.com&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Film Maker IQ&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Film Maker IQ is a group of filmmakers who discuss a range of topics. With articles on things such as Make-Up Tutorials to Camera comparisons, they answer both the&lt;em&gt;whys&lt;/em&gt;and hows of filmmaking and help us understand the new media wave, without forgetting the old.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;View&lt;a title="Film Maker IQ" href="http://www.filmmakeriq.com/" target="_blank"&gt;filmmakeriq.com&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Who did we miss?&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Add your favourite filmmaking website in the comments box below.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style="text-align: center;"&gt;

             <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-29897">
              <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-29897">
               <footer class="comment-meta">
                <div class="comment-author vcard">
                 <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-96 photo avatar-default" height="96" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="96"/>
                 <cite class="fn">
                  <a class="url" href="http://www.facebook.com/lorenzo.barzanti" rel="external nofollow">
                   Lorenzo Barzanti
                  </a>
                 </cite>
                 <span class="says">
                  says:
                 </span>
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-author -->
                <div class="comment-metadata">
                 <a href="http://www.raindance.org/top-13-sites-for-independent-filmmakers/#comment-29897">
                  <time datetime="2013-08-27T13:56:14+00:00">
                   August 27, 2013 at 1:56 pm
                  </time>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-metadata -->
               </footer>
               <!-- .comment-meta -->
               <div class="comment-content">
                <p>
                 Hi,
                </p>
                <p>
                 we're writing to inform you about the Nordic Creative Commons Film Festival. The NCCFF is coming (30th of August  8th of September) and we have launched a CC Video Remix Competition for the Festival. Professional and amateur filmmakers, everywhere, are invited to submit their short video remixing content from the film program together with additional Creative Commons or public domain material.The winners will receive a cash award of 3000 SEK each! Get all the details about the contest on the web and show us your creativity!
                 <br/>
                 Please have a look here if you want to know more about the REMIX Competition:
                 <br/>
                 <a href="http://www.nordicfilmfestival.cc/?page_id=530" rel="nofollow">
                  http://www.nordicfilmfestival.cc/?page_id=530
                 </a>
                </p>
                <p>
                 If you have further question or if you have any problem write us:
                 <a href="mailto:info@nordicfilmfestival.cc">
                  info@nordicfilmfestival.cc
                 </a>
                 .
                </p>
                <p>
                 We really hope you enjoy yourself.
                 <br/>
                 Greetings
                </p>
               </div>

                 Hey buddies, check out my campaign for my film Kelza 55  a thriller about motorcycle gangs in San Francisco.
                 <a href="http://www.indiegogo.com/projects/kelza-55/x/5742516" rel="nofollow">
                  http://www.indiegogo.com/projects/kelza-55/x/5742516
                 </a>
                </p>

               <!-- .comment-meta -->
               <div class="comment-content">
                <p>
                 CINE is now accepting submissions for the Spring 2014 CINE Golden Eagle Awards! Since 1957, CINE's prestigious Golden Eagle Award has represented excellence in the film and TV industry; notable alumni include Steven Spielberg, Ken Burns, Mel Brooks and Pixar Animation (and many others). Submit your film by February 21 and save some money on your entry fee; all entries are due by March 7. For more information on the Golden Eagle Award eligibility and submission categories for professional, emerging and student filmmakers, visit
                 <a href="http://www.cine.org" rel="nofollow">
                  http://www.cine.org
                 </a>
                 or Withoutabox. Questions? Email us at
                 <a href="mailto:info@cine.org">
                  info@cine.org
                 </a>
                 .
                </p>
               </div>

                  says:
                 </span>
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-author -->
                <div class="comment-metadata">
                 <a href="http://www.raindance.org/top-13-sites-for-independent-filmmakers/#comment-44077">
                  <time datetime="2014-02-19T12:28:56+00:00">
                   February 19, 2014 at 12:28 pm
                  </time>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-metadata -->
               </footer>
               <!-- .comment-meta -->
               <div class="comment-content">
                <p>
                 Hi!
                 <br/>
                 Met Film School in London has got these two weekend-courses that I would love to recommend (filmmaking). The school is located ten minutes walking distance from the station: Ealing Broadway. The famous studio "Ealing studios" is right next to the school. Maybe you can meet up with Daniel Radcliffe after school?
                </p>
                <p>
                 Never done anything with filmmaking before? Then you should apply for the course: DSLR for professional filmmaking. It is a weekend course that is designed for those with a working understanding of the principals of cinematography or stills photography that want to apply this knowledge specifically to shooting with digital SLR cameras. You will learn how to get the best from a DSLR camera and how to make use of a selection of accessories specifically designed for video shootings on stills cameras. Through a range of creative exercises you will discover the pros and cons of working with these systems and how to avoid some of the most common pitfalls.
                </p>
                <p>
                 Done some filmmaking before? Do you want something more advanced? You should apply for our course: Advanced DSLR for professional filmmaking. This course is designed for students who have previously completed the DSLR for professional filmmaking course, or those with an extensive DSLR and/or cinematography background. This programme covers areas from focus and operating, to sound sync and postproduction workflows. The aim of this programme is to provide you with the fundamental knowledge to shoot and finish DSLR video footage to its highest standard.
                </p>
                <p>
                 Apply now on their website:
                 <a href="http://www.metfilmschool.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">
                  http://www.metfilmschool.co.uk/
                 </a>
                </p>
               </div>
               <!-- .comment-content -->

                 CINEMA FROM AZORES
                </p>
                <p>
                 An experimental spiritual film from Aores shot in the volcanic island of So Miguel.
                </p>

                </p>

                 <a href="https://vimeo.com/deepchat/filmloveisblind" rel="nofollow">

                 <a href="http://www.raindance.org/top-13-sites-for-independent-filmmakers/#comment-70045">
                  <time datetime="2014-10-05T16:52:05+00:00">
                   October 5, 2014 at 4:52 pm
                  </time>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <!-- .comment-metadata -->
               </footer>
               <!-- .comment-meta -->
               <div class="comment-content">
                <p>
                 Looking for film location rentals? Check out
                 <a href="http://www.filmlocationswanted.com" rel="nofollow">
                  http://www.filmlocationswanted.com
                 </a>
                 website. They list location rentals from all over the world. You can search for a location on the website and contact the owners directly to discuss your needs. A free resource. You can also contact FLW with a location inquiry for your project and they will send out to their community of owners looking to rent their homes and businesses for production.
                </p>
               </div>

                <p>
                 Heaven | The First War
                </p>
                <p>
                 A project that requires support.
                 <br/>
                 I recommend attending a film animation that takes into account exceptional presentation to the Creation event.
                 <br/>
                 The project requires funding for trailer presentation will then go into production.
                 <br/>
                 You can support with a donation on Kickstarter or distributing delving further this post.
                 <br/>
                 The history of this film we can write together!
                </p>
